<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718"></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2">
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Cameron Jibril Thomaz</b> (born September 8, 1987),<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> better known by his stage name <b>Wiz Khalifa</b>, is an American rapper. He released his debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Show_and_Prove" title="Show and Prove">Show and Prove</a></i>, in 2006 and signed to <a href="/wiki/Warner_Records" title="Warner Records">Warner Bros. Records</a> in 2007. His <a href="/wiki/Eurodance" title="Eurodance">Eurodance</a>-influenced single "<a href="/wiki/Say_Yeah_(Wiz_Khalifa_song)" title="Say Yeah (Wiz Khalifa song)">Say Yeah</a>" received <a href="/wiki/Urban_radio" class="mw-redirect" title="Urban radio">urban radio</a> airplay, charting on the <a href="/wiki/Rhythmic_Top_40" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhythmic Top 40">Rhythmic Top 40</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hot_Rap_Tracks" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot Rap Tracks">Hot Rap Tracks</a> charts in 2008, becoming his first minor hit.<sup id="cite_ref-ErieTimesNews_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ErieTimesNews-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Thomaz parted ways with Warner Bros. and released his second album, <i><a href="/wiki/Deal_or_No_Deal_(album)" title="Deal or No Deal (album)">Deal or No Deal</a></i>, independently in November 2009. He released the mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/Kush_and_Orange_Juice" class="mw-redirect" title="Kush and Orange Juice">Kush and Orange Juice</a></i> as a free download in April 2010; he then signed with <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Records" title="Atlantic Records">Atlantic Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Thomaz then adopted an <a href="/wiki/Urban_contemporary_music" title="Urban contemporary music">urban</a> <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a>-influenced approach with his debut single for Atlantic, "<a href="/wiki/Black_and_Yellow" title="Black and Yellow">Black and Yellow</a>". The song, a tribute to his hometown of <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a>, debuted at number 100 and eventually reached number 1 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, also earning him two <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> nominations. "Black and Yellow" became the lead single for his third album <a href="/wiki/Rolling_Papers_(Wiz_Khalifa_album)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rolling Papers (Wiz Khalifa album)"><i>Rolling Papers</i></a>, which was released in March 2011, and also contained the <a href="/wiki/Top_40" title="Top 40">Top 40</a> singles "<a href="/wiki/Roll_Up_(Wiz_Khalifa_song)" title="Roll Up (Wiz Khalifa song)">Roll Up</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/No_Sleep_(Wiz_Khalifa_song)" title="No Sleep (Wiz Khalifa song)">No Sleep</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The album's success was followed up with <i><a href="/wiki/O.N.I.F.C." title="O.N.I.F.C.">O.N.I.F.C.</a></i> in December 2012, which was backed by the singles "<a href="/wiki/Work_Hard,_Play_Hard" title="Work Hard, Play Hard">Work Hard, Play Hard</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Remember_You" title="Remember You">Remember You</a>" (featuring <a href="/wiki/The_Weeknd" title="The Weeknd">the Weeknd</a>). Thomaz released his fifth album <i><a href="/wiki/Blacc_Hollywood" title="Blacc Hollywood">Blacc Hollywood</a></i> in August 2014; it became his first album peak atop the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> and was preceded by the lead single "<a href="/wiki/We_Dem_Boyz" title="We Dem Boyz">We Dem Boyz</a>". In March 2015, he released "<a href="/wiki/See_You_Again" title="See You Again">See You Again</a>" (featuring <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Puth" title="Charlie Puth">Charlie Puth</a>) for the soundtrack of the film <i><a href="/wiki/Furious_7" title="Furious 7">Furious 7</a></i> and the song  peaked the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> for 12 non-consecutive weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-seeyouagainbillboard_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seeyouagainbillboard-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Outside of music, Thomaz has acted in television series such as <i><a href="/wiki/Punk%27d" title="Punk&#39;d">Punk'd</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Dickinson_(TV_series)" title="Dickinson (TV series)"><i>Dickinson</i></a>, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Eric_Andre_Show" title="The Eric Andre Show">The Eric Andre Show</a></i>, as well as having voice roles in animated series such as <i><a href="/wiki/American_Dad!" title="American Dad!">American Dad!</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Duncanville_(TV_series)" title="Duncanville (TV series)">Duncanville</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Big_City_Greens" title="Big City Greens">Big City Greens</a></i>. He has also founded the company <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Gang_Entertainment" title="Taylor Gang Entertainment">Taylor Gang Entertainment</a> in 2008, a record label that has signed artists such as <a href="/wiki/Juicy_J" title="Juicy J">Juicy J</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ty_Dolla_Sign" title="Ty Dolla Sign">Ty Dolla Sign</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Berner_(rapper)" title="Berner (rapper)">Berner</a>, among others. Known for his abundant usage of <a href="/wiki/Cannabis" title="Cannabis">cannabis</a>, Thomaz released his own cannabis brand, Khalifa Kush, in 2016, which expanded to release in nationwide dispensaries in 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<p>Khalifa was born Cameron Jibril Thomaz on September 8, 1987, in <a href="/wiki/Minot,_North_Dakota" title="Minot, North Dakota">Minot, North Dakota</a>, to parents serving in the <a href="/wiki/Military_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of the United States">military</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ErieTimesNews_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ErieTimesNews-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> His parents divorced when Khalifa was about three years old. He was a <a href="/wiki/Military_brat_(U.S._subculture)" title="Military brat (U.S. subculture)">military brat</a>, frequently moving around with his parents' military service. Khalifa lived in <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> before settling in <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a> with his mother in around 1996 where he attended <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Allderdice_High_School" title="Taylor Allderdice High School">Taylor Allderdice High School</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ErieTimesNews_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ErieTimesNews-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WizKhalifaDay_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WizKhalifaDay-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Soon after moving to Pittsburgh, Khalifa began to write and perform his own lyrics before he was a teenager.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>His stage name is derived from <a href="/wiki/Khalifa" title="Khalifa">Khalifa</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> word meaning "successor", and <a href="/wiki/Wisdom" title="Wisdom">wisdom</a>, which was shortened to Wiz when Khalifa was a young boy.<sup id="cite_ref-Brotha_Ash_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brotha_Ash-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Khalifa stated to <a href="/wiki/Spinner_(website)" title="Spinner (website)">Spinner.com</a> that the name also came from being called "young Wiz 'cause I was good at everything I did, and my granddad is <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a>, so he gave me that name; he felt like that's what I was doing with my music." He got a tattoo of his stage name on his 17th birthday.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By the age of 15, he was regularly recording his music at a local studio called <a href="/wiki/I.D._Labs" class="mw-redirect" title="I.D. Labs">I.D. Labs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Wiz_Khalifa_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wiz_Khalifa-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Impressed by the young teen's talent, E. Dan, the owner of the studio offered Khalifa an intern job at the studio in exchange for free recording time. Dan, being a veteran of the Pittsburgh hip-hop scene, would help develop and mentor the young artist early on in his career.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-Wiz_Khalifa_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wiz_Khalifa-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span></h2>
<h3><span id="2005.E2.80.932008:_Early_mixtapes_and_Show_and_Prove"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2005–2008:_Early_mixtapes_and_Show_and_Prove">2005–2008: Early mixtapes and <i>Show and Prove</i></span></h3>
<p>Rostrum Records president Benjy Grinberg first heard about Wiz Khalifa in 2004 when the rapper's contribution to a mixtape of various new Pittsburgh artists attracted his interest.<sup id="cite_ref-hitquarters.com_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hitquarters.com-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> When Grinberg finally met the 16-year-old artist, he immediately decided he wanted to work with him, later telling <a href="/wiki/HitQuarters" title="HitQuarters">HitQuarters</a>: "Even though he wasn't all the way developed you could just tell that he was a diamond in the rough, and that with some polishing, guidance and backing he could become something special." Khalifa signed to the label shortly after and began a seven-year period of artist development.<sup id="cite_ref-hitquarters.com_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hitquarters.com-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Khalifa released his first <a href="/wiki/Mixtape" title="Mixtape">mixtape</a>, <i>Prince of the City: Welcome to Pistolvania</i>, in 2005. The mixtape paved the way for his first full-length album entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Show_and_Prove" title="Show and Prove">Show and Prove</a></i> in 2006. Khalifa was declared an "artist to watch" that year in <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hiphopdx.com_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphopdx.com-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2007, Khalifa signed to <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Warner Bros. Records">Warner Bros. Records</a> and released two mixtapes through <a href="/wiki/Rostrum_Records" title="Rostrum Records">Rostrum Records</a>: <i>Grow Season</i>, hosted by <a href="/wiki/DJ_Green_Lantern" title="DJ Green Lantern">DJ Green Lantern</a> and released on July 4, 2007, and <i>Prince of the City 2</i>, released on November 20, 2007. His debut Warner Bros. single "<a href="/wiki/Say_Yeah_(Wiz_Khalifa_song)" title="Say Yeah (Wiz Khalifa song)">Say Yeah</a>" reached number 25 on the <i>Billboard</i> <a href="/wiki/Rhythmic_Top_40" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhythmic Top 40">Rhythmic Top 40</a> music chart and number 20 on <i>Billboard's</i> <a href="/wiki/Hot_Rap_Tracks" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot Rap Tracks">Hot Rap Tracks</a>. The song <a href="/wiki/Sampling_(music)" title="Sampling (music)">samples</a> "<a href="/wiki/Better_Off_Alone_(Alice_DeeJay_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Better Off Alone (Alice DeeJay song)">Better Off Alone</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Alice_Deejay" title="Alice Deejay">Alice Deejay</a>. Khalifa's vocals from "Say Yeah" appear near the end of Pittsburgh <a href="/wiki/Mashup_(music)" title="Mashup (music)">mashup</a> producer <a href="/wiki/Girl_Talk_(musician)" title="Girl Talk (musician)">Girl Talk</a>'s 2008 album, <i><a href="/wiki/Feed_the_Animals" title="Feed the Animals">Feed the Animals</a></i>, over music from <a href="/wiki/Underworld_(band)" title="Underworld (band)">Underworld's</a> "<a href="/wiki/Born_Slippy" class="mw-redirect" title="Born Slippy">Born Slippy</a>", <a href="/wiki/Usher_(entertainer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Usher (entertainer)">Usher's</a> "<a href="/wiki/Love_in_This_Club" title="Love in This Club">Love in This Club</a>", and <a href="/wiki/The_Cure" title="The Cure">the Cure</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/In_Between_Days" title="In Between Days">In Between Days</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Khalifa appeared with <a href="/wiki/The_Game_(rapper)" title="The Game (rapper)">The Game</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Banner" title="David Banner">David Banner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Play-n-Skillz" class="mw-redirect" title="Play-n-Skillz">Play-n-Skillz</a> at <a href="/wiki/KUUU" title="KUUU">U92's</a> Summer Jam at the <a href="/wiki/USANA_Amphitheatre" title="USANA Amphitheatre">USANA Amphitheatre</a> in <a href="/wiki/West_Valley_City,_Utah" title="West Valley City, Utah">West Valley City</a>, Utah on August 2, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Khalifa released the mixtapes <i>Star Power</i> in September 2008, and <i><a href="/wiki/Flight_School_(album)" class="mw-redirect" title="Flight School (album)">Flight School</a></i> in April 2009 on Rostrum Records.
</p><p>Khalifa parted ways with <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Warner Bros. Records">Warner Bros. Records</a> in July 2009 after numerous delays in releasing his planned debut album for the label, <i>First Flight</i>. Khalifa stated to the <i><a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Post-Gazette" title="Pittsburgh Post-Gazette">Pittsburgh Post-Gazette</a></i> that, "I learned a lot during my time there and matured as an artist during the process. I'm happy to be moving on with all of my material and having the chance to be in control of my next moves".<sup id="cite_ref-PostGazette-July2009_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PostGazette-July2009-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Khalifa appeared with Girl Talk, <a href="/wiki/Modey_Lemon" title="Modey Lemon">Modey Lemon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Donora_(band)" title="Donora (band)">Donora</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grand_Buffet" title="Grand Buffet">Grand Buffet</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Don_Caballero" title="Don Caballero">Don Caballero</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Amphitheatre_at_Station_Square" class="mw-redirect" title="Amphitheatre at Station Square">Amphitheatre at Station Square</a> in Pittsburgh on July 31, 2009, where he announced that his relationship with Warner Bros. was over.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2009.E2.80.932010:_Deal_or_No_Deal_and_signing_with_Atlantic_Records"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2009–2010:_Deal_or_No_Deal_and_signing_with_Atlantic_Records">2009–2010: <i>Deal or No Deal</i> and signing with Atlantic Records</span></h3>
<p>Continuing his association with Rostrum Records, Khalifa released the single "Teach U to Fly", and the mixtape <i>How Fly</i>, a collaboration with New Orleans rapper <a href="/wiki/Curren$y" class="mw-redirect" title="Curren$y">Curren$y</a>, on August 9, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-PostGazette-July2009_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PostGazette-July2009-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Khalifa introduced a more melodic style on the mixtape, alternating between singing and rapping. He opened for <a href="/wiki/Wu-Tang_Clan" title="Wu-Tang Clan">Wu-Tang Clan</a> member <a href="/wiki/U-God" title="U-God">U-God</a> at the 2009 <a href="/wiki/CMJ_Music_Marathon" class="mw-redirect" title="CMJ Music Marathon">CMJ Music Marathon</a> in New York City. Khalifa released the mixtape <i>Burn After Rolling</i> on November 2, 2009, where he raps over familiar beats from other artists, including the songs "<a href="/wiki/If_I_Were_A_Boy" class="mw-redirect" title="If I Were A Boy">If I Were A Boy</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Diva_(Beyonc%C3%A9_Knowles_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Diva (Beyoncé Knowles song)">Diva</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Walking_on_a_Dream_(song)" title="Walking on a Dream (song)">Walking on a Dream</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_the_Sun_(band)" title="Empire of the Sun (band)">Empire of the Sun</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Luchini_AKA_This_Is_It" title="Luchini AKA This Is It">Luchini AKA This Is It</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Camp_Lo" title="Camp Lo">Camp Lo</a>, and  "<a href="/wiki/Best_I_Ever_Had_(Drake_song)" title="Best I Ever Had (Drake song)">Best I Ever Had</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Drake_(entertainer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Drake (entertainer)">Drake</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mccray_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mccray-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Khalifa released his second album, <i><a href="/wiki/Deal_or_No_Deal_(album)" title="Deal or No Deal (album)">Deal or No Deal</a></i>, on November 24, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Khalifa performed at <a href="/wiki/Emo%27s" title="Emo&#39;s">Emo's</a> in <a href="/wiki/Austin,_Texas" title="Austin, Texas">Austin</a>, Texas in March 2010 as part of the 2010 <a href="/wiki/South_by_Southwest" title="South by Southwest">South by Southwest</a> Music Festival.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> He appeared on the cover of <i><a href="/wiki/XXL_(magazine)" title="XXL (magazine)">XXL</a></i> magazine that same month, for the magazine's annual list of Top 10 Freshman, which included <a href="/wiki/Donnis" title="Donnis">Donnis</a>, <a href="/wiki/J._Cole" title="J. Cole">J. Cole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pill_(rapper)" title="Pill (rapper)">Pill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Gibbs" title="Freddie Gibbs">Freddie Gibbs</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fashawn" title="Fashawn">Fashawn</a>. Wiz Khalifa was named 2010 "Rookie Of The Year" by "<a href="/wiki/The_Source_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Source (magazine)">The Source</a>", with alongside Rick Ross, "The Man Of The Year".<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> He toured with rapper <a href="/wiki/Yelawolf" title="Yelawolf">Yelawolf</a> on a 20-date tour, the Deal Or No Deal Tour.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Khalifa released the free mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/Kush_and_Orange_Juice" class="mw-redirect" title="Kush and Orange Juice">Kush and Orange Juice</a></i> for download on June 14, 2010. Due to Khalifa's devoted grassroots fan base, the mixtape became the No. 1 <a href="/wiki/Trending_topic" class="mw-redirect" title="Trending topic">trending topic</a> on Twitter with the <a href="/wiki/Hash_tag" class="mw-redirect" title="Hash tag">hash tag</a> #kushandorangejuice, and "Kush and Orange Juice download" ranked No. 1 on <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>'s hot search trends.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Citing music industry insiders, <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_(magazine)" title="New York (magazine)">New York</a></i> magazine wrote that Khalifa signed with <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Records" title="Atlantic Records">Atlantic Records</a> in April 2010, although the rapper did not confirm it.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> He stated to <a href="/wiki/AllHipHop" title="AllHipHop">AllHipHop</a> in June 2010 that he was working on a new album, but was weighing his options and had not yet decided on a label to distribute it. Khalifa confirmed to MTV on July 30 that he was signing an Atlantic Records deal.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiz_Khalifa_Boston_Urban_Music_Project_August_2010.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="Wiz Khalifa on stage" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Wiz_Khalifa_Boston_Urban_Music_Project_August_2010.jpg/250px-Wiz_Khalifa_Boston_Urban_Music_Project_August_2010.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Wiz_Khalifa_Boston_Urban_Music_Project_August_2010.jpg/375px-Wiz_Khalifa_Boston_Urban_Music_Project_August_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Wiz_Khalifa_Boston_Urban_Music_Project_August_2010.jpg/500px-Wiz_Khalifa_Boston_Urban_Music_Project_August_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a><figcaption>Wiz Khalifa on stage in <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a> in August 2010</figcaption></figure>
<p>Khalifa was featured in a remix and video for the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rick Ross (rapper)">Rick Ross</a> single "<a href="/wiki/Super_High" title="Super High">Super High</a>", alongside <a href="/wiki/Curren$y" class="mw-redirect" title="Curren$y">Curren$y</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> He guested on the mixtape <i>Grey Goose, Head Phones, and Thirsty Women </i> by <a href="/wiki/St._Louis" title="St. Louis">St. Louis</a> rapper M.C,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> and was featured on the track "The Breeze (Cool)" on rapper <a href="/wiki/Wale_(rapper)" title="Wale (rapper)">Wale</a>'s August 2010 mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/More_About_Nothing" class="mw-redirect" title="More About Nothing">More About Nothing</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Khalifa was named MTV's Hottest Breakthrough MC of 2010, winning with nearly 70,000 votes, and beating out finalists <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a>, <a href="/wiki/J._Cole" title="J. Cole">J. Cole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Travis_Porter" title="Travis Porter">Travis Porter</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Diggy_Simmons" title="Diggy Simmons">Diggy Simmons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Khalifa appeared at the Soundset 2010 festival in May 2010 in <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis" title="Minneapolis">Minneapolis</a>, Minnesota, alongside <a href="/wiki/Method_Man_%26_Redman" title="Method Man &amp; Redman">Method Man &amp; Redman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Del_the_Funky_Homosapien" title="Del the Funky Homosapien">Del the Funky Homosapien</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hieroglyphics_(group)" title="Hieroglyphics (group)">Hieroglyphics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere_(music_group)" title="Atmosphere (music group)">Atmosphere</a>, <a href="/wiki/Murs_(rapper)" title="Murs (rapper)">Murs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cage_(rapper)" title="Cage (rapper)">Cage</a>, and others.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> He performed at the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Rock_the_Bells" title="Rock the Bells">Rock the Bells</a> festival, along with hip hop veterans Wu-Tang Clan, <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lauryn_Hill" title="Lauryn Hill">Lauryn Hill</a>, <a href="/wiki/A_Tribe_Called_Quest" title="A Tribe Called Quest">A Tribe Called Quest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rakim" title="Rakim">Rakim</a>, <a href="/wiki/KRS-One" title="KRS-One">KRS-One</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jedi_Mind_Tricks" title="Jedi Mind Tricks">Jedi Mind Tricks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slick_Rick" title="Slick Rick">Slick Rick</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Khalifa declined an invitation to tour with rapper <a href="/wiki/Drake_(entertainer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Drake (entertainer)">Drake</a> and launched his own Waken Baken Tour, a 50-city national tour with rapper <a href="/wiki/Yelawolf" title="Yelawolf">Yelawolf</a>. His official DJ on the tour was <a href="/wiki/DJ_Bonics" title="DJ Bonics">DJ Bonics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Whirl2010_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Whirl2010-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The tour, scheduled to last from September to November 2010, sold out every venue. In November 2010, during his "Waken Baken" tour at East Carolina University, Khalifa was arrested for possession and trafficking of marijuana. He was released the next morning after a $300K bail, and resumed his tour. Khalifa performed in a cypher during the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Black_Entertainment_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Entertainment Television">BET</a> Hip-Hop Awards.
</p>
<h3><span id="2010.E2.80.932012:_Mainstream_success.2C_Rolling_Papers_and_O.N.I.F.C."></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2010–2012:_Mainstream_success,_Rolling_Papers_and_O.N.I.F.C.">2010–2012: Mainstream success, <i>Rolling Papers</i> and <i>O.N.I.F.C.</i></span></h3>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiz_Khalifa_SXSW_2010.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Wiz_Khalifa_SXSW_2010.jpg/180px-Wiz_Khalifa_SXSW_2010.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="247" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Wiz_Khalifa_SXSW_2010.jpg/270px-Wiz_Khalifa_SXSW_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Wiz_Khalifa_SXSW_2010.jpg/360px-Wiz_Khalifa_SXSW_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="746" data-file-height="1024" /></a><figcaption>Wiz Khalifa at <a href="/wiki/South_by_Southwest" title="South by Southwest">SXSW</a> in 2010</figcaption></figure>
<p>Khalifa released "<a href="/wiki/Black_and_Yellow" title="Black and Yellow">Black and Yellow</a>", his first single for Rostrum/Atlantic, produced by <a href="/wiki/Stargate_(production_team)" class="mw-redirect" title="Stargate (production team)">Stargate</a>, which has received radio airplay.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The single peaked at number one on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>; the title of the song refers to the colors of the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Pittsburgh" class="mw-redirect" title="City of Pittsburgh">City of Pittsburgh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-lipshutz_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lipshutz-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Khalifa released his debut album with Atlantic Records in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> He appeared with Curren$y on the track "Scaling the Building" on producer <a href="/wiki/Ski_Beatz" title="Ski Beatz">Ski Beatz</a>' 2010 album, <i><a href="/wiki/24_Hour_Karate_School" title="24 Hour Karate School">24 Hour Karate School</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 29, 2011, Khalifa released his first studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Papers_(Wiz_Khalifa_album)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rolling Papers (Wiz Khalifa album)">Rolling Papers</a></i> in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The album debuted at number two on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart, with first-week sales of 197,000 copies in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> On March 31, 2011, Khalifa performed at <a href="/wiki/Emory_University" title="Emory University">Emory University</a> in Atlanta, Georgia as part of the school's annual Dooley's Weekend. On June 26, 2011, Khalifa was nominated and won Best New Artist at the <a href="/wiki/BET_Awards_of_2011" class="mw-redirect" title="BET Awards of 2011">BET Awards of 2011</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Khalifa collaborated with British rapper <a href="/wiki/Tinie_Tempah" title="Tinie Tempah">Tinie Tempah</a>. Tinie announced in an interview with <a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a> that his next single is to be called "<a href="/wiki/Till_I%27m_Gone" title="Till I&#39;m Gone">Till I'm Gone</a>" and would feature Wiz Khalifa and was produced by <a href="/wiki/Stargate_(production_team)" class="mw-redirect" title="Stargate (production team)">Stargate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The single and the video song were released at the end of June 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 11, 2012, Khalifa announced that he will release his second studio album titled <i>Only Nigga In First Class</i> but that it will be abbreviated as <i><a href="/wiki/O.N.I.F.C." title="O.N.I.F.C.">O.N.I.F.C.</a></i> for release to mainstream markets.<sup id="cite_ref-hiphopdx.com_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphopdx.com-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> <i>O.N.I.F.C.</i> debuted at number two with 131,000 in first week sales.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The album has spawned two singles "<a href="/wiki/Work_Hard,_Play_Hard" title="Work Hard, Play Hard">Work Hard, Play Hard</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Remember_You" title="Remember You">Remember You</a>" both receiving good commercial acclaim and the former going platinum. Wiz spoke with rapper <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a>, with whom he collaborated on the song "Telescope", about making a movie together.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2013.E2.80.93present:_Blacc_Hollywood_and_Rolling_Papers_2"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2013–present:_Blacc_Hollywood_and_Rolling_Papers_2">2013–present: <i>Blacc Hollywood</i> and <i>Rolling Papers 2</i></span></h3>
<p>In April 2013, Khalifa revealed that after having his son he decided to work on a new album that he was planning to release in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> On April 17, 2013, Wiz Khalifa and Curren$y announced that they will drop their collaboration <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">EP</a> <i>Live in Concert</i> on April 20, 2013. The EP featured seven new songs.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> On June 24, 2013, he announced that his fifth studio album would be titled <i><a href="/wiki/Blacc_Hollywood" title="Blacc Hollywood">Blacc Hollywood</a></i> and would be released in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-rap-up1_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rap-up1-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> On September 3, 2013, Khalifa revealed he had recorded songs with <a href="/wiki/Miley_Cyrus" title="Miley Cyrus">Miley Cyrus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Juicy_J" title="Juicy J">Juicy J</a> for <i>Blacc Hollywood</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> In October 2013, <a href="/wiki/Mannie_Fresh" title="Mannie Fresh">Mannie Fresh</a> confirmed that he provided production for the album.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 11, 2014, Khalifa released <i>Blacc Hollywood</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s first single titled "<a href="/wiki/We_Dem_Boyz" title="We Dem Boyz">We Dem Boyz</a>". On March 31, 2015, Wiz Khalifa released an <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">EP</a> with fellow Taylor Gang artist <a href="/wiki/Ty_Dolla_Sign" title="Ty Dolla Sign">Ty Dolla $ign</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Talk_About_It_in_the_Morning" title="Talk About It in the Morning">Talk About It in the Morning</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> That same month, Khalifa and <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Puth" title="Charlie Puth">Charlie Puth</a> released the song "<a href="/wiki/See_You_Again" title="See You Again">See You Again</a>", a tribute to <a href="/wiki/Paul_Walker" title="Paul Walker">Paul Walker</a>, who died during filming for <i><a href="/wiki/Furious_7" title="Furious 7">Furious 7</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-seeyouagainbillboard_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seeyouagainbillboard-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiz_Khalifa_High_Road.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Wiz_Khalifa_High_Road.jpg/220px-Wiz_Khalifa_High_Road.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="210" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Wiz_Khalifa_High_Road.jpg/330px-Wiz_Khalifa_High_Road.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Wiz_Khalifa_High_Road.jpg/440px-Wiz_Khalifa_High_Road.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1517" data-file-height="1446" /></a><figcaption>Khalifa performing in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>, July 2016</figcaption></figure>
<p>After releasing several "Weedmixes" on <a href="/wiki/SoundCloud" title="SoundCloud">SoundCloud</a>, including "Ziplocc"<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> and "Maan!",<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Wiz took to Twitter to create hype about his new mixtape, <i><a href="/wiki/28_Grams" title="28 Grams">28 Grams</a></i>, which was due to be released on May 25, 2014. However, Wiz was arrested in <a href="/wiki/El_Paso,_Texas" title="El Paso, Texas">El Paso, Texas</a> for marijuana possession the day before, and there were fears that the mixtape would be pushed back. After posting a "jail selfie" and <a href="/wiki/Hashtag" title="Hashtag">hashtagging</a> "FreeTrapWiz" on Twitter, he was released hours later, meaning the mixtape would go ahead with its intended release date.
</p><p>On January 23, 2015, Khalifa was featured on a remix release of the <a href="/wiki/Fall_Out_Boy" title="Fall Out Boy">Fall Out Boy</a> song "<a href="/wiki/Uma_Thurman_(song)" title="Uma Thurman (song)">Uma Thurman</a>". On May 18, they performed the song together on the 2015 <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Music_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Billboard Music Award"><i>Billboard</i> Music Awards</a> show.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> In the summer of 2015, he began touring the United States with <a href="/wiki/Fall_Out_Boy" title="Fall Out Boy">Fall Out Boy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hoodie_Allen" title="Hoodie Allen">Hoodie Allen</a> in a tour titled "<a href="/wiki/American_Beauty/American_Psycho_Tour#Tour_dates" title="American Beauty/American Psycho Tour">The Boys of Zummer Tour</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The tour featured performances of "Uma Thurman" by Fall Out Boy and Khalifa. Later that year, on December 15, 2015, Wiz released the mixtape "<a href="/wiki/Cabin_Fever_3_(mixtape)" title="Cabin Fever 3 (mixtape)">Cabin Fever 3</a>". During the Golden Globes on January 10, 2016, Wiz announced that his next album, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Khalifa_(album)" title="Khalifa (album)">Khalifa</a></i>, would be released on the 22nd of that month.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> However, the album was released on February 5, 2016. On May 24, 2016, he released "Pull Up", a standalone single in promotion of his sixth album, Rolling Papers 2,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> which was released on July 13, 2018.
</p><p>In 2016, Khalifa sued former manager Benjy Grinberg and <a href="/wiki/Rostrum_Records" title="Rostrum Records">Rostrum Records</a> because of a "<a href="/wiki/360_deal" title="360 deal">360 deal</a>" that he signed which he claimed was unfair.<sup id="cite_ref-Former_Manager_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Former_Manager-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Khalifa is seeking $1 million in compensation as well as punitive damages and attorney fees. He and Grinberg split after 10 years of partnership.<sup id="cite_ref-Former_Manager_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Former_Manager-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2018, he wrote racist and offensive lyrics about Koreans in his song "Hot Now", sparking controversy.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 20, 2020, Khalifa released a new EP, The Saga of Wiz Khalifa. The album included collaborations with <a href="/wiki/Tyga" title="Tyga">Tyga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Logic_(rapper)" title="Logic (rapper)">Logic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mustard_(record_producer)" title="Mustard (record producer)">Mustard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ty_Dolla_Sign" title="Ty Dolla Sign">Ty Dolla $ign</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2020, Khalifa featured on a new song, <i>Drums Drums Drums</i> with <a href="/wiki/Travis_Barker" title="Travis Barker">Travis Barker</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2021, Khalifa competed in <a href="/wiki/The_Masked_Singer_(American_season_5)" title="The Masked Singer (American season 5)">season five</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Masked_Singer_(American_TV_series)" title="The Masked Singer (American TV series)">The Masked Singer</a></i> as "Chameleon". He finished in third place.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>Khalifa began dating model <a href="/wiki/Amber_Rose" title="Amber Rose">Amber Rose</a> in early 2011. They got engaged on March 1, 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> and married on July 8, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> They have one son, Sebastian Taylor (born 2013).<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> On September 24, 2014, it was announced that Rose would be filing for divorce, citing <a href="/wiki/Irreconcilable_differences" title="Irreconcilable differences">irreconcilable differences</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> As of 2015, Khalifa and Rose have <a href="/wiki/Joint_custody_(United_States)" title="Joint custody (United States)">joint custody</a> of their son.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Khalifa is open about his use of <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_(drug)" title="Cannabis (drug)">cannabis</a>, and he has claimed in many interviews that he spends $10,000 a month on cannabis, and also smokes daily.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> As of early 2014, Khalifa no longer pays for cannabis and is sponsored by The Cookie Company, a medical marijuana dispensary which sells his "Khalifa Kush" (KK) strain, which he partnered with RiverRock Cannabis to create.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Also, in 2016 Khalifa was featured in a cooking show with <a href="/wiki/Martha_Stewart" title="Martha Stewart">Martha Stewart</a> and <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a> where weed was the main ingredient.
</p><p>Khalifa began training in the martial art <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_jiu-jitsu" title="Brazilian jiu-jitsu">Brazilian jiu-jitsu</a> in May 2017 with <a href="/wiki/Rigan_Machado" title="Rigan Machado">Rigan Machado</a>, an 8th degree red and black belt.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Shortly after, he began training in <a href="/wiki/Muay_Thai" title="Muay Thai">Muay Thai</a> with former <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_Fighting_Championship" title="Ultimate Fighting Championship">UFC</a> bantamweight title contender <a href="/wiki/Cat_Zingano" title="Cat Zingano">Cat Zingano</a> and at the Unbreakable Performance Center in Los Angeles.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> On April 24, 2018, <a href="/wiki/Yokkao" title="Yokkao">Yokkao</a> hosted a private Muay Thai seminar with Thai boxing legend <a href="/wiki/Saenchai" title="Saenchai">Saenchai</a> for Khalifa at Unbreakable.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2023, it was announced that Khalifa would be taking on his first BJJ match against an unconfirmed opponent under the High Rollerz ruleset.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honors">Honors</span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_City_Council" title="Pittsburgh City Council">Pittsburgh City Council</a> declared 12-12-12 (December 12, 2012) to be Wiz Khalifa Day in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-WizKhalifaDay_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WizKhalifaDay-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Khalifa graduated from Pittsburgh's Taylor Allderdice High School<sup id="cite_ref-WizKhalifaDay_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WizKhalifaDay-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> and in January 2012, purchased a home in nearby <a href="/wiki/Canonsburg,_Pennsylvania" title="Canonsburg, Pennsylvania">Canonsburg, Pennsylvania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Machosky_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Machosky-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CBShome2012_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBShome2012-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<ul><li><span class="nowrap">"<a href="/wiki/When_You_Believe" title="When You Believe">When You Believe</a>" – Music and Lyrics by <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Schwartz_(composer)" title="Stephen Schwartz (composer)">Stephen Schwartz</a> (1998)</span></li>

<li><span class="nowrap">"<a href="/wiki/May_It_Be" title="May It Be">May It Be</a>" – Music and Lyrics by <a href="/wiki/Enya" title="Enya">Enya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicky_Ryan" title="Nicky Ryan">Nicky Ryan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roma_Ryan" title="Roma Ryan">Roma Ryan</a> / "<a href="/wiki/Vanilla_Sky_(song)" title="Vanilla Sky (song)">Vanilla Sky</a>" – Music and Lyrics by <a href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney" title="Paul McCartney">Paul McCartney</a> (2001)</span></li>
